Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[Brahman.тАФcaturviс╣Е┼Ыakam. ─Бrс╣гabham. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 8. bhurij; 6, 10, 24. jagat─л; 11-17, 19, 20, 23. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 18. upariс╣гс╣н─Бd bс╣Ыhat─л; 21. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti.]

Whitney

Comment

Found also in P─Бipp. xvi. (in the verse-order 1-3, 5, 4, 6, 8, 7, 9, 10-13, 15, 14, 16-22, 24, 23). Not noticed in V─Бit., and not in K─Бu┼Ы. in a way to cast any light whatever upon it; the hymn is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 19 (with vi. 111) in the ceremony of turning a bull loose, and vs. 24 separately in the same ceremony in K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 21; also vs. 1 in 66. 18 in connection with a bull; the hymn is reckoned (see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 19. 1) among the puс╣гс╣нika mantras.

Translations

Translated: Henry, 90, 128; Griffith, i. 438.тАФFor some of the vss. the reader may consult Hillebrandt, Ved. Myth. i. 330, 516, 382, 358, 525.

Griffith

A glorification of the typical sacrificial bull

Whitney
Translation
  1. The bright bull of a thousand, rich in milk, bearing all forms in his
    bellies, desiring to accomplish (? ┼Ыikс╣г) what is excellent for his
    giver, the sacrificerтАФhe, the ruddy one of Brihaspati, hath stretched
    тМК─Б-tanтМЛ the line (t├бntu).
Notes

That is, doubtless, ‘has extended or performed the sacrifice.’

Griffith

The Bull, fierce, thousandfold, filled full of vigour, bearing within his flanks all forms and natures, Brihaspati’s Steer, hath stretched the thread, bestowing bliss on the worshipper, the liberal giver.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who in the beginning became the counterpart (pratim─Б╠Б) of the
    waters, prevailing (prabh┼л╠Б) for everything, like the divine earth,
    father of young (vats├б), lord of the inviolable [kine]тАФlet him set
    (kс╣Ы) us in thousandfold prosperity.
Notes
Griffith

He who at first became the Waters’ model, a match for everyone, like Earth the Goddess; The husband of the cows, the young calves’ father, may be secure us thousandfold abundance.

Translation
  1. A male (p├║m─Бс╣Еs), [yet] pregnant, big (sth├бvira), rich in milk,

Griffith

Masculine, pregnant, stedfast. full of vigour, the Bull sustains a trunk of goodly treasure. May Agni Jatavedas bear him offered, on pathways traversed by the Gods, to Indra.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Father of calves, lord of the inviolable [kine], also father of
    great gulfs (g├бrgara); calf, afterbirth, fresh milk, beestings, curd,
    gheeтАФthat [is] his seed.
Notes

The verse occurs also in TS. (iii. 3. 9┬▓), MS. (ii. 5. 10), and K.
(xiii. 9). In b, MS. reads ut─Б╠Б тАЩy├бm for ├бtho; for d, TS. has

r├йtaс╕е.

Griffith

The husband of the cows, the young calves’ father, father is he of mighty water-eddies. Calf, after-birth, new milk drawn hot, and biestings, curds, butter, that is his best genial humour.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The gods’ portion [was] that load, the sap of waters, of plants,
    of ghee; the mighty one (┼Ыakr├б) chose a drink of soma; a great stone
    became what [was his] body.
Notes

This verse also is found in TS. and MS. (as above), in both texts
preceding our vs. 4 (in MS. one other verse intervenes, our xviii. 4.
28). Both have, for a, dev─Б╠Бn─Бm eс╣г├б upan─Бh├б ─Бs─лt; for b, TS.
has ap─Б╠Бс╣Б g├бrbha ├│с╣гah─лс╣гu ny├аktaс╕е, and MS. ap─Б╠Бm p├бtir vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б
├│с╣гadh─лn─Бm; in c, both have draps├бm for bhakс╣г├бm and p┼лс╣г─Б╠Б for
┼Ыakr├бс╕е; in d, after abhavat, MS. has y├бt t├бd ─Б╠Бs─лt, and TS.
t├бd eс╣г─Бm.

Griffith

He is the Gods’ allotted share and bundle, essence of waters, and of plants, and butter. Sakra elected him, the draught of Soma. What was his body was a lofty mountain.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou bearest a vessel filled with soma, shaper (tv├бstс╣Ы) of forms,
    generator of cattle; propitious to thee be these pudenda (? prajan┼л╠Б)
    that are here; to us, O ax, confirm those that are yonder.
Notes

Ppp. reads at the beginning somasya; its second half-verse is
unintelligible. The verse is with no propriety called a jagat─л (11 +
11: 13 + 12 = 47).

Griffith

A beaker filled with Soma juice thou bearest. framer of forms, begetter of the cattle. Kindly to us be these thy wombs here present, and stay for us, O Axe, those that are yonder.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Sacrificial butter he bears; ghee [is] his seed; thousandfold
    prosperityтАФthat they call the sacrifice; the bull, clothing himself in
    Indra’s formтАФlet him, O gods, come propitious to us, being given.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b sahasrapoс╣гas, and in d тАШsm─Б and ┼Ыiv─Бi тАЩtu.

Griffith

He bears oblation, and his seed is butter. Thousand-fold plenty; sacrifice they call him. May he, the Bull, wearing the shape of Indra, come unto us, O Gods, bestowed, with blessing.

  1. Indra’s force, Varuс╣Зa’s two arms, the A┼Ыvins’ two shoulders, of the
    Maruts this hump; they who are wise, poets, who are skilful (man─лс╣г├нn),

The verse has two jagat─л-p─Бdas, though called by the Anukr. simply
bhurij. Read at the end of b kak├║t.

Griffith

Both arms of Varuna, and Indra’s vigour, the Maruts’ hump is he, the Asvins’ shoulders. They who are sages, bards endowed with wisdom, call him Brihaspati compact and heightened.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Rich in milk, thou stretchest unto the people (v├н┼Ы) of the gods;
    thee they call Indra, thee Sarasvant; he gives a thousand [kine] with
    one face who makes offering (─Б-hu) of a bull to a Brahman.
Notes

тМКCf. Oldenberg, IFA. vi. 183.тМЛ

Griffith

Thou, vigorous, reachest to the tribes of heaven. Thee they call Indra, thee they call Sarasvan. Turned to one aim, that Brahman gives a thousand who offers up the Bull as his oblation.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Brihaspati, Savitar bestowed on thee vigor (v├бyas); from Tvashс╣нar,
    from V─Бyu was brought forth thy soul (─Бtm├бn); with mind in the
    atmosphere I make offering (hu) of thee; let heaven-and-earth both be
    thy barh├нs.
Notes

Ppp. reads manas for vayas in a. The Anukr. calls the verse
jagat─л, though two of its p─Бdas are triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

Brihaspati, Savitar gave thee vital vigour: thy breath was brought from Tvashtar and from Vayu. In thought I offer thee in air’s mid-region. Thy sacrificial grass be Earth and Heaven!

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - [рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп !] (рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдХреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдиреЗ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЕрдиреНрди [рд╡рд╛ рдмрд▓] (рджрдзреМ) рджрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯреБрдГ) рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ (рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рд╕реЗ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░рд╛ (рдЖрддреНрдорд╛) рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ (рдкрд░рд┐) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ (рдЖрднреГрддрдГ) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рд╣реИред (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ) рд╕рдм рдореЗрдВ рджреАрдЦрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреБрдЭрдХреЛ (рдордирд╕рд╛) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ (рдЬреБрд╣реЛрдорд┐) рдореИрдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ, (рдЙрднреЗ) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдФрд░ рднреВрдорд┐ (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рдГ) рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ (рд╕реНрддрд╛рдореН) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрежрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Translation
  1. His rump was the ─Аdityas’; his two thighs were Brihaspati’s; his
    tail [was] the heavenly wind’s; therewith he shakes the herbs.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b ┼Ыroс╣З─лy ─Бst─Бm.

Griffith

The Adityas claim the hinder parts, the loins must be Brihas- pati’s. Vata, the God, receives the tail: he stirs the plants and herbs therewith,

Whitney
Translation
  1. His breast (kroс╕Н├б) was J─Бmi┼Ыaс╣Еsa’s; his vessel [was] maintained
    as Soma’s, when all the gods, coming together, distributed
    (vi-kalpay-) the bull.
Notes

We had j─Бmi┼Ыaс╣Еsa above (ii. 10. 1) as ‘imprecation of sisters’; the
word does not occur elsewhere. What part of the bull is his ‘vessel’ is
obscure. The first p─Бda has a redundant syllable.

Griffith

They made a jest of kindred’s curse: a jar of Soma juice was set, What time the deities, convened, assigned the Bull’s divided parts.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Those dew-claws (k├║с╣гс╣нhik─Б) [were] Saram─Б’s; they assigned the
    hoofs to the tortoises (k┼лrm├б); the content of his bowels they
    maintained for the worms, the ┼Ыavart├бs.
Notes

The mss. are divided between ┼Ыavarta (P.s.m.I.O.R.p.m.T.D.Kp.) and
┼Ыvavarta (Bp.E.R.s.m.); while M. and P.p.m. have ┼Ыva┼Ыavarta, and W.
┼Ыa┼Ыavarta. The occurrence of ┼Ыavart├б in TS. (v. 7. 23┬╣: also in
connection with ┼л╠Бbadhya) determined the reading of our text. But our
pada-text divides the word (Bp. ┼Ыvaре░vart├б; D.Kp. ┼Ыaре░v-), which
favors the reading ┼Ыva-, since it implies a combination of the two
recognizably independent words ┼Ыvan and varta, ‘occurring in dogs,’
or something of the sort. Ppp. apparently has ┼Ыivaratrebhyo. тМКRoth
suggests that ┼Ыavarta may be for ┼Ыavavarta ‘Aaswurm, Made.’тМЛ

Griffith

They gave the hooves to tortoises, to Sarama scraps of the feet: His undigested food they gave to worms and things that creep and crawl.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Having given a bull to Brahmans, one makes his mind wider; he
    beholds (ava-pa┼Ы) prosperity of the inviolable [kine] in his own
    stall.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a br─Бhmaс╣З─Бya vс╣Ыс╣гabhaс╣Б, and in d vi pa┼Ыyatu. In
a, we have to combine (as not very rarely elsewhere) -bhya rс╣г-.

Griffith

He who hath given away the Bull to Brahmans frees and cheers his soul. In his own cattle-pen he sees the growth and increase of his cows.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let this burly (p├нp─Бna) one, a very Indra, bestow conspicuous
    wealth; let this one [bestow] a well-milking cow, constantly with
    calf; let him yield (duh) inspired will beyond the sky.
Notes

Ppp. has very different readings, which in part are less unacceptable
than those of our text: for a, b, ayaс╣Б pip─Бn─Б indriyaс╣Б gay─Бс╣Б
bibharti tejan─л: in d, vipa┼Ыyataс╣Б puro divaс╕е. тМКFor p├нp─Бna, cf.
Bloomfield, AJP. xii. 443.тМЛ

Griffith

Indra here verily hath rejoiced: let him bestow conspicuous wealth. May he draw forth at will from yonder side of heaven a deft cow, good to milk, whose calf is never wanting.

реиреи рдкрд┐рд╢рдЩреНрдЧрд░реВрдкреЛ рдирднрд╕реЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Of reddish form, clouded (? nabhas├б), vigor-giving, vehemence of
    Indra, all-formed, he hath come to us, assigning to us life-time and
    progeny; and with abundances of wealth let him attach himself to
    (abhi-sac) us.
Notes

The last half-verse agrees nearly with xviii. 4. 62 c, d, where
d├бdhatas and sacadhvam make better meter. It is not impossible to
resolve asm├бbhi-am in c, but sacant─Бm, which some of the mss.
read (P.p.m.W.D.), is forbidden by the sense. Ppp. has a wholly
different line: praj─Бm asmabhyaс╣Б dadhato rayiс╣Б ca d─лrgh─Бyutv─Бya
┼Ыata┼Ы─Бrad─Бya. тМКBloomfield translates the verse at ZDMG. xlviii. 566,
but overlooks the accent of nabhas├│: cf. t├бmas-─Б and tamas─Б╠Б
(saс╣Бhit─Б-form at xi. 9. 22).тМЛ

Griffith

With close connexion mingle with the cows in this our cattle- pen: Mingle, the Bull’s prolific flow, and, Indra! thine heroic strength!

Griffith

Here we restore this Bull, your youthful leader: sporting with him, go, wander at your pleasure. Ne’er, wealthy ones! may he be reft of offspring; and do ye favour us with growth of riches.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This young male we set toward you here; with him go ye (fem.)
    playing according to your wills; abandon us not with birth, ye
    wellportioned ones; and with abundances of wealth attach yourselves to
    us.
Notes

The last p─Бda is the same with xviii. 4. 62 d. The verse is found,
in much more acceptable form, in TS. (iii. 3. 9┬╣, followed, after one
intervening verse, by our vss. 5, 4 above) and PGS. (iii. 9. 6,
disagreeing with TS. in only one word); they read, for a, et├бс╣Б
y├║v─Бnam p├бri (but PGS. patiс╣Б) vo dad─Бmi (omitting atra); in
b, priy├йс╣Зa for v├б┼Ы─Бс╣Е ├бnu; in c, ┼Ы─Бpta for h─Бsiс╣гс╣нa; and,
for d, r─Бy├бs p├│с╣гeс╣Зa s├бm iс╣г─Б╠Б madema (nearly our iii. 15. 8 c).
Ppp. agrees with our text, only combining dadhmo тАШtra in a. But
for the accent of jan├║с╣г─Б (in TS. also), we might render, with
Stenzler, ‘ye who are by birth well-portioned.’ Bp.R.p.m. have at end of
c subhag─Бs. The Anukr. weakly calls the verse (12 + 12: 11 + 11) a
jagat─л, in spite of the triс╣гс╣нubh cadence of its first p─Бda. It is
quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 21, to accompany the sending away of an older bull
and the release of a new one. тМКSee also note to K─Бu┼Ы. 25. 24.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the second anuv─Бka with 2 hymns and 55 verses. The quoted
Anukr. says “s─Бhasre"тМЛ
